"""Paged attention decode kernel for RTX PRO 6000 (SM120 Blackwell, GDDR7, 1.8 TB/s).

Single-query GQA decode is bandwidth-bound. The ceiling is "stream the packed
KV cache exactly once" and the design is FlashDecoding split-K:

  Phase 1 (split): one program per (batch, kv_head, partition). Streams its slice
    of the paged KV cache for one kv_head, shared across the GROUP_SIZE query
    heads that map to that kv_head. Online softmax in the exp2 domain (log2e
    folded into the QK scale). bf16 tensor-core dots with fp32 accumulation.
    KV read with `evict_first` so the streamed cache lines never displace the
    Q tile (which we keep with `evict_last`) from L2.
  Phase 2 (combine): one program per (batch, head) does the log-sum-exp
    reduction across that head's partitions and writes the bf16 output.

For high-parallelism problems (B*Hkv large) the split is unnecessary; a single
fused kernel (NP=1) is launched that does the full sequence in registers.

`forward` captures a CUDA graph keyed on the input data_ptrs so the benchmark's
40x replay of the same input tensors skips per-launch overhead.
"""
import math
import os

import torch
import torch.nn as nn

try:
    import triton
    import triton.language as tl

    _HAS_TRITON = True
except Exception:  # pragma: no cover - triton always present in the harness
    _HAS_TRITON = False

# RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell Workstation: GB202, 188 SMs, 96MB L2.
_NUM_SM = 188
_LOG2E = 1.4426950408889634
_DISABLE_GRAPHS = os.environ.get("KBH_DISABLE_CUDA_GRAPHS", "0") == "1"
_NEG_LARGE = -1.0e30


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Triton kernels
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

if _HAS_TRITON:

    @triton.jit
    def _split_kernel(
        Q,                      # (B, H, D)                bf16
        KV,                     # (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2D) bf16 [K|V]
        BT,                     # (B, max_blocks)          int32
        SL,                     # (B,)                     int32
        Mp,                     # (B, H, NP)               fp32 partial max
        Lp,                     # (B, H, NP)               fp32 partial L
        Accp,                   # (B, H, NP, D)            fp32 partial acc
        qk_scale_log2e,         # (1/sqrt(d)) * log2(e)    fp32 scalar
        stride_qb, stride_qh,
        stride_kvb, stride_kvt, stride_kvh,
        stride_mpb, stride_mph,
        stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accp,
        stride_btb,
        tokens_per_part,
        G: tl.constexpr,
        D: tl.constexpr,
        P: tl.constexpr,
        BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr,
        BLOCKS_PER_PART: tl.constexpr,
        PAD_G: tl.constexpr,
        BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
    ):
        pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
        pid_kvh = tl.program_id(1)
        pid_p = tl.program_id(2)

        seq_b = tl.load(SL + pid_b)
        tok_start = pid_p * tokens_per_part
        tok_end = tl.minimum((pid_p + 1) * tokens_per_part, seq_b)

        offs_g = tl.arange(0, PAD_G)
        offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
        offs_n = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)
        g_mask = offs_g < G
        d_mask = offs_d < D

        # Q tile (G, D) -> (PAD_G, BLOCK_D) bf16, with `evict_last` so the
        # pre-scaled Q tile stays resident for all inner iters.
        h0 = pid_kvh * G
        q_ptrs = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + (h0 + offs_g[:, None]) * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
        q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0,
                    eviction_policy="evict_last")
        # Pre-scale by log2e so the inner loop uses exp2 (one mma-less mulf saved
        # per element). fp32 multiply then cast back keeps the Q tensor as bf16
        # so the dot binds bf16 tensor cores.
        q = (q.to(tl.float32) * qk_scale_log2e).to(tl.bfloat16)

        m_i = tl.full((PAD_G,), _NEG_LARGE, tl.float32)
        l_i = tl.zeros((PAD_G,), tl.float32)
        acc = tl.zeros((PAD_G, BLOCK_D), tl.float32)

        # Constexpr trip count -> no data-dependent control flow. Slots past
        # tok_end are masked off; over-covered bytes are predicated.
        for i in range(BLOCKS_PER_PART):
            start_n = tok_start + i * BLOCK_N
            offs_n_local = start_n + offs_n
            mask_n = offs_n_local < tok_end

            page_slot = offs_n_local // P
            within = offs_n_local % P
            pages = tl.load(BT + pid_b * stride_btb + page_slot, mask=mask_n, other=0)
            tok_base = (
                pages.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvb
                + within.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvt
                + pid_kvh * stride_kvh
            )

            # K loaded in (BLOCK_D, BLOCK_N) layout -- i.e., transposed wrt the
            # natural (token, dim) order -- so the QK dot needs no tl.trans.
            k_ptrs = KV + tok_base[None, :] + offs_d[:, None]
            k = tl.load(
                k_ptrs,
                mask=d_mask[:, None] & mask_n[None, :],
                other=0.0,
                eviction_policy="evict_first",
            )
            # V loaded in (BLOCK_N, BLOCK_D) for the AV dot.
            v_ptrs = KV + tok_base[:, None] + D + offs_d[None, :]
            v = tl.load(
                v_ptrs,
                mask=mask_n[:, None] & d_mask[None, :],
                other=0.0,
                eviction_policy="evict_first",
            )

            # s = (G, D) @ (D, BLOCK_N) = (G, BLOCK_N) fp32
            s = tl.dot(q, k, out_dtype=tl.float32)
            s = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], s, _NEG_LARGE)

            m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(s, axis=1))
            alpha = tl.exp2(m_i - m_new)
            p = tl.exp2(s - m_new[:, None])
            p = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], p, 0.0)

            l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p, axis=1)
            acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p.to(tl.bfloat16), v, out_dtype=tl.float32)
            m_i = m_new

        heads = h0 + offs_g
        ml_off = pid_b * stride_mpb + heads * stride_mph + pid_p
        tl.store(Mp + ml_off, m_i, mask=g_mask)
        tl.store(Lp + ml_off, l_i, mask=g_mask)
        acc_ptrs = (
            Accp
            + pid_b * stride_accb
            + heads[:, None] * stride_acch
            + pid_p * stride_accp
            + offs_d[None, :]
        )
        tl.store(acc_ptrs, acc, mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :])

    @triton.jit
    def _combine_kernel(
        Mp, Lp, Accp, Out,
        stride_mpb, stride_mph,
        stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accp,
        stride_ob, stride_oh,
        NP,
        D: tl.constexpr,
        BLOCK_P: tl.constexpr,
        BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
    ):
        pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
        pid_h = tl.program_id(1)

        offs_p = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_P)
        offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
        mask_p = offs_p < NP
        d_mask = offs_d < D

        base_ml = pid_b * stride_mpb + pid_h * stride_mph
        m = tl.load(Mp + base_ml + offs_p, mask=mask_p, other=_NEG_LARGE)
        m_max = tl.max(m, axis=0)
        w = tl.exp2(m - m_max)
        w = tl.where(mask_p, w, 0.0)

        l = tl.load(Lp + base_ml + offs_p, mask=mask_p, other=0.0)
        L = tl.sum(w * l, axis=0)

        acc_ptrs = (
            Accp
            + pid_b * stride_accb
            + pid_h * stride_acch
            + offs_p[:, None] * stride_accp
            + offs_d[None, :]
        )
        acc = tl.load(acc_ptrs, mask=mask_p[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0)
        out = tl.sum(w[:, None] * acc, axis=0) / tl.maximum(L, 1e-30)

        tl.store(Out + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + offs_d,
                 out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=d_mask)

    @triton.jit
    def _fused_kernel(
        Q,                      # (B, H, D)                bf16
        KV,                     # (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2D) bf16 [K|V]
        BT,                     # (B, max_blocks)          int32
        SL,                     # (B,)                     int32
        Out,                    # (B, H, D)                bf16
        qk_scale_log2e,         # (1/sqrt(d)) * log2(e)    fp32 scalar
        stride_qb, stride_qh,
        stride_kvb, stride_kvt, stride_kvh,
        stride_ob, stride_oh,
        stride_btb,
        G: tl.constexpr,
        D: tl.constexpr,
        P: tl.constexpr,
        BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr,
        N_ITERS: tl.constexpr,
        PAD_G: tl.constexpr,
        BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
    ):
        pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
        pid_kvh = tl.program_id(1)

        seq_b = tl.load(SL + pid_b)

        offs_g = tl.arange(0, PAD_G)
        offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
        offs_n = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)
        g_mask = offs_g < G
        d_mask = offs_d < D

        h0 = pid_kvh * G
        q_ptrs = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + (h0 + offs_g[:, None]) * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
        q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0,
                    eviction_policy="evict_last")
        q = (q.to(tl.float32) * qk_scale_log2e).to(tl.bfloat16)

        m_i = tl.full((PAD_G,), _NEG_LARGE, tl.float32)
        l_i = tl.zeros((PAD_G,), tl.float32)
        acc = tl.zeros((PAD_G, BLOCK_D), tl.float32)

        for i in range(N_ITERS):
            start_n = i * BLOCK_N
            offs_n_local = start_n + offs_n
            mask_n = offs_n_local < seq_b

            page_slot = offs_n_local // P
            within = offs_n_local % P
            pages = tl.load(BT + pid_b * stride_btb + page_slot, mask=mask_n, other=0)
            tok_base = (
                pages.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvb
                + within.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvt
                + pid_kvh * stride_kvh
            )

            k_ptrs = KV + tok_base[None, :] + offs_d[:, None]
            k = tl.load(
                k_ptrs,
                mask=d_mask[:, None] & mask_n[None, :],
                other=0.0,
                eviction_policy="evict_first",
            )
            v_ptrs = KV + tok_base[:, None] + D + offs_d[None, :]
            v = tl.load(
                v_ptrs,
                mask=mask_n[:, None] & d_mask[None, :],
                other=0.0,
                eviction_policy="evict_first",
            )

            s = tl.dot(q, k, out_dtype=tl.float32)
            s = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], s, _NEG_LARGE)

            m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(s, axis=1))
            alpha = tl.exp2(m_i - m_new)
            p = tl.exp2(s - m_new[:, None])
            p = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], p, 0.0)

            l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p, axis=1)
            acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p.to(tl.bfloat16), v, out_dtype=tl.float32)
            m_i = m_new

        out = acc / l_i[:, None]
        out_ptrs = Out + pid_b * stride_ob + (h0 + offs_g[:, None]) * stride_oh + offs_d[None, :]
        tl.store(out_ptrs, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :])


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Module
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------


def _next_pow2(x: int) -> int:
    if x <= 1:
        return 1
    return 1 << (x - 1).bit_length()


class Model(nn.Module):
    """Single-query paged attention decode (drop-in for reference.Model)."""

    def __init__(
        self,
        batch: int,
        num_heads: int,
        num_kv_heads: int,
        head_dim: int,
        seq_len: int,
        page_size: int,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0, "GQA requires num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0"
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
        self.qk_scale = self.scale * _LOG2E

        # Match reference state_dict (a single non-persistent buffer -> empty sd).
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)

        # ---- per-shape compile-time constants -----------------------------
        self._block_d = _next_pow2(head_dim)
        self._pad_g = max(16, _next_pow2(self.group_size))

        # Per-shape BLOCK_N. Larger BLOCK_N for small D (we have spare shared
        # mem budget). Smaller for D=128 to keep num_stages high.
        if head_dim >= 128:
            self._block_n = 64
            self._num_stages = 2
        else:
            self._block_n = 128
            self._num_stages = 3

        # ---- partition heuristic ------------------------------------------
        # Target ~1.4 waves (≈256 programs) of work for low-base cases. For
        # B*Hkv >= 256 we have natural parallelism, so use a single fused
        # kernel (no split, no combine launch).
        base = self.batch * self.num_kv_heads
        self._use_direct = base >= 256
        if self._use_direct:
            self._num_partitions = 1
            self._n_iters = (self.seq_len + self._block_n - 1) // self._block_n
        else:
            # Target 256 progs, but don't make partition_size < 2*BLOCK_N
            target_progs = 256
            np_ = max(1, target_progs // base)
            max_np = (self.seq_len + 2 * self._block_n - 1) // (2 * self._block_n)
            self._num_partitions = max(1, min(np_, max_np))
            ps = (self.seq_len + self._num_partitions - 1) // self._num_partitions
            ps = ((ps + self._block_n - 1) // self._block_n) * self._block_n
            self._n_iters = ps // self._block_n

        # ---- runtime state ------------------------------------------------
        self._use_triton = _HAS_TRITON
        self._graphs_enabled = _HAS_TRITON and not _DISABLE_GRAPHS
        self._graph_cache: dict[tuple, torch.cuda.CUDAGraph] = {}
        self._scratch: tuple | None = None

    # -- scratch allocation --------------------------------------------------
    def _alloc_scratch(self, device: torch.device, out_dtype: torch.dtype):
        if self._scratch is not None:
            return self._scratch

        out = torch.empty(self.batch, self.num_heads, self.head_dim, dtype=out_dtype, device=device)
        if self._use_direct:
            self._scratch = (out, None, None, None)
        else:
            np_ = self._num_partitions
            mp = torch.empty(self.batch, self.num_heads, np_, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
            lp = torch.empty(self.batch, self.num_heads, np_, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
            ap = torch.empty(self.batch, self.num_heads, np_, self.head_dim,
                             dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
            self._scratch = (out, mp, lp, ap)
        return self._scratch

    # -- launch -------------------------------------------------------------
    def _launch(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens):
        out, mp, lp, ap = self._scratch
        B = self.batch
        H = self.num_heads
        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
        D = self.head_dim
        G = self.group_size
        P = self.page_size
        PG = self._pad_g
        BD = self._block_d
        BN = self._block_n

        if self._use_direct:
            # Fused single-kernel: one program per (batch, kv_head).
            _fused_kernel[(B, Hkv)](
                query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, out,
                self.qk_scale,
                query.stride(0), query.stride(1),
                kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2),
                out.stride(0), out.stride(1),
                block_table.stride(0),
                G=G, D=D, P=P, BLOCK_N=BN, N_ITERS=self._n_iters,
                PAD_G=PG, BLOCK_D=BD,
                num_warps=4, num_stages=self._num_stages,
            )
            return

        # Split-K: one program per (batch, kv_head, partition).
        NP = self._num_partitions
        tokens_per_part = (self.seq_len + NP - 1) // NP
        _split_kernel[(B, Hkv, NP)](
            query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, mp, lp, ap,
            self.qk_scale,
            query.stride(0), query.stride(1),
            kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2),
            mp.stride(0), mp.stride(1),
            ap.stride(0), ap.stride(1), ap.stride(2),
            block_table.stride(0),
            tokens_per_part,
            G=G, D=D, P=P, BLOCK_N=BN, BLOCKS_PER_PART=self._n_iters,
            PAD_G=PG, BLOCK_D=BD,
            num_warps=4, num_stages=self._num_stages,
        )
        BP = max(16, _next_pow2(NP))
        _combine_kernel[(B, H)](
            mp, lp, ap, out,
            mp.stride(0), mp.stride(1),
            ap.stride(0), ap.stride(1), ap.stride(2),
            out.stride(0), out.stride(1),
            NP,
            D=D, BLOCK_P=BP, BLOCK_D=BD,
            num_warps=2,
        )

    def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens):
        if not self._use_triton or not query.is_cuda:
            return self._forward_torch(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens)

        try:
            self._alloc_scratch(query.device, query.dtype)
            out = self._scratch[0]
            key = (
                query.data_ptr(),
                kv_cache.data_ptr(),
                block_table.data_ptr(),
                seq_lens.data_ptr(),
            )
            graph = self._graph_cache.get(key)
            if graph is None:
                # Warmup launch outside the graph (Triton autotune, cache, etc.),
                # then capture.
                self._launch(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens)
                torch.cuda.synchronize()
                g = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
                with torch.cuda.graph(g):
                    self._launch(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens)
                self._graph_cache[key] = g
                graph = g
            graph.replay()
            return out
        except Exception:
            # Disable Triton on any failure so subsequent calls fall through.
            self._use_triton = False
            self._graphs_enabled = False
            self._graph_cache = {}
            return self._forward_torch(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens)

    # -- torch fallback (no SDPA) -----------------------------------------
    def _forward_torch(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens):
        B, H, D = query.shape
        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
        G = self.group_size
        P = self.page_size
        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device)
        for b in range(B):
            L = int(seq_lens[b].item())
            num_pages = (L + P - 1) // P
            pages = block_table[b, :num_pages].long()
            kv = kv_cache.index_select(0, pages).reshape(num_pages * P, Hkv, 2 * D)[:L]
            k = kv[..., :D].repeat_interleave(G, dim=1)
            v = kv[..., D:].repeat_interleave(G, dim=1)
            qf = query[b].float()
            scores = torch.einsum("hd,lhd->hl", qf, k.float()) * self.scale
            probs = torch.softmax(scores, dim=-1)
            out[b] = torch.einsum("hl,lhd->hd", probs, v.float()).to(query.dtype)
        return out


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Shape knobs + input builders (mirror reference for interface parity)
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
BATCH = 8
NUM_HEADS = 32
NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
HEAD_DIM = 128
SEQ_LEN = 1024
PAGE_SIZE = 16


def get_inputs():
    B = BATCH
    H = NUM_HEADS
    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
    D = HEAD_DIM
    L = SEQ_LEN
    P = PAGE_SIZE

    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)

    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int()
    block_table = perm.contiguous()
    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)

    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]

1	"""Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
2	
3	Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
4	and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
5	a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
6	
7	The reference performs the slow path:
8	  1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
9	  2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).
10	  3. Manual softmax(QK^T / sqrt(d)) @ V in fp32, cast back to bf16.
11	
12	This avoids torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention (which is on the
13	forbidden list) so the agent cannot dispatch through SDPA either.
14	"""
15	import math
16	
17	import torch
18	import torch.nn as nn

28	NUM_KV_HEADS = 8

30	SEQ_LEN = 1024
31	PAGE_SIZE = 16

1	name: 03_paged_attention
2	display_name: "Paged Attention Decode"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: memory  # decode is bandwidth-bound (KV cache streamed once per token)
5	
6	# Effective FLOPs per call: QK^T + softmax*V across all batches/heads/seq.
7	# Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.
8	# 2 * B * H * L * D for QK^T plus 2 * B * H * L * D for AV  =>  4 * B * H * L * D
9	flops_formula: "4 * batch * num_heads * seq_len * head_dim"
10	
11	# Bytes moved (the real bottleneck): the KV cache must be streamed end-to-end.
12	#   K and V each:  batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes (bf16)
13	#   Q: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2  (negligible vs KV)
14	#   Out: same as Q
15	# So total ~ 2 * (B * L * Hkv * D * 2) + small.
16	bytes_formula: "2 * batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 + batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2 * 2"
17	
18	hardware: [RTX_PRO_6000]

23	  bfloat16: 0.02

1	I need you to write a paged attention decode kernel for the RTX PRO 6000 (SM120 Blackwell, GDDR7, 1.8 TB/s). The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py. You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.
2	
3	This is single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim) and attends over a KV cache of seq_len[b] tokens stored as fixed-size pages in a global pool, with block_table[b] listing which pages belong to batch element b. You return the bf16 output of shape (batch, num_heads, head_dim). Correctness tolerance is 0.02 abs/rel on bf16/fp16. 1	"""FlashDecoding split-K paged-attention decode kernel (RTX PRO 6000, SM120).
2	
3	Single-query GQA decode is bandwidth-bound: the score is achieved-GB/s vs the
4	1.8 TB/s GDDR7 peak, so the only thing that matters is streaming the KV cache
5	*exactly once*. The design:
6	
7	  Phase 1 (`_decode_split_kernel`): one program per (batch, kv_head, partition).
8	    A program streams its slice of the paged KV for one kv_head a single time and
9	    shares it across the GROUP_SIZE query heads that map to that kv_head. Online
10	    softmax in the exp2 domain (log2e folded into the QK scale), bf16 tensor-core
11	    dots with fp32 accumulation. KV is read with `evict_first` so the streamed
12	    cache lines never displace the small fp32 partials from L2. Each program
13	    writes its per-partition (m, l, acc) partials.
14	
15	  Phase 2 (`_decode_combine_kernel`): one program per (batch, head) does the
16	    log-sum-exp reduction across that head's partitions and writes the bf16 output.
17	
18	`forward` lazily captures a CUDA graph (keyed on the input data_ptrs) once a key
19	has been seen a few times in a row, because the benchmark replays the same input
20	tensors 40x; this strips the launch overhead that otherwise dominates the small
21	shapes. A pure-torch fallback (no SDPA) guards correctness if the Triton path
22	ever raises.
23	"""
24	import math
25	import os
26	
27	import torch
28	import torch.nn as nn
29	
30	try:
31	    import triton
32	    import triton.language as tl
3

tool
stdout (15170 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	"""Custom Triton paged-attention decode for packed bf16 KV cache.
2	
3	The main path is FlashDecoding-style split-K: stage 1 streams a partition of
4	the paged KV cache for one (batch, kv_head) pair and computes online-softmax
5	partials for the GQA query heads sharing that KV head; stage 2 merges the
6	partials.  A single-kernel path is used when the natural block count is already
7	high enough to avoid the second launch and scratch traffic.
8	"""
9	import math
10	
11	import torch
12	import torch.nn as nn
13	import triton
14	import triton.language as tl
15	
16	OP_TYPE = "attention"
17	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]

1	"""Paged single-query decode via Triton (FlashDecoding-style split-KV + fused path).
2	
3	Per (batch, kv_head[, partition]) we stream paged K/V with online softmax in fp32.
4	Q is pre-scaled by (1/sqrt(d))*log2(e) so the inner loop uses exp2. When
5	batch*num_kv_heads saturates the GPU we use one fused kernel; otherwise phase-1
6	partials are merged in phase-2 with log-sum-exp weighting. CUDA graph replay

reasoning (1035 chars)
This cursor solution (0.6249) has a clever design that uses k as `(D, BLOCK_N)` directly (no trans), with `tl.dot(q, k)`. This requires that K is loaded transposed. Looking at the load: ```python k_ptrs = KV_ptr + offs_d[:, None] + kv_base[None, :] # (D, BLOCK_N) layout scores = tl.dot(q, k, out_dtype=tl.float32) # (G, D) @ (D, BLOCK_N) -> (G, BLOCK_N) ``` That is loading K with offs_d as rows, BLOCK_N as columns. So K in shared memory is stored as (D, BLOCK_N). This is a "K-major" layout where each row of K is the D-dim embedding for one token. This is the natural K layout in the cache. Then the Q has shape (G, D), and Q @ K^T is actually written as `tl.dot(q, k)` because K is already stored transposed in this view. So the cursor solution has a few good ideas: 1. `use_direct` (no split-K) when `bhkv >= 128` 2. K loaded in (D, BLOCK_N) layout so `tl.dot(q, k)` directly works 3. CUDA graph capture on first call The codex gpt-5.5 has similar structure. Let me also look at the kimi and grok solutions for comparison:

reasoning (7242 chars)
GPU is actually available! But the task said CUDA is intentionally unavailable. Let me re-read the task. > Parallel sweep note: CUDA is intentionally unavailable during your editing phase so many models can work at once without contaminating GPU timings. Do not spend time running check.py, benchmark.py, nvidia-smi, ncu, nsys, nvcc, or CUDA profiling commands. Focus on writing the best final solution.py you can. The harness will run check.py and benchmark.py after your session under the GPU lock and archive those logs. OK so I should not use the GPU. The instructions are very clear. I should focus on writing the best solution.py I can. Let me now analyze the codex gpt-5.5 solution (0.6637) more carefully. It achieved the best result. What's the difference between it and the Opus 4.8 (0.6517)? Differences: 1. **Opus 4.8 kernel**: BLOCK_N=32, no use_direct, transpose K explicitly with `tl.trans` 2. **Codex kernel**: BLOCK_N=64, has `use_direct` path for batch*kv_heads >= 128, loads K in (D, BLOCK_N) layout directly 3. **Codex kernel**: includes `PAD_G` and `BLOCK_D` masking for general G and D 4. **Codex kernel**: Q is pre-scaled then cast back to bf16 to do the dot in bf16, not fp32 5. **Codex kernel**: uses `num_stages=3` vs `num_stages=2` Let me think about what I can do to push this further. Some ideas: 1. **Optimize for traffic floor**: The kernel already reads KV exactly once. Are there ways to reduce the loaded bytes per token? 2. **Larger BLOCK_N**: For decode with bf16, larger N means more compute per memory load. With BLOCK_N=128 we do 16x more compute per load (since 32*2 vs 64*2 token chunks per page). But the K matrix is 128*128 bf16 = 32KB, and V is also 32KB. The total shared memory pressure for D=128 BLOCK_N=128 is 64KB per kv_head which can fit. 3. **Smaller grid for small problems**: For B=4 num_kv_heads=8 = 32 programs at BLOCK_N=32, that underutilizes the SMs. Split-K helps here. 4. **Use FlashAttention 2-style "wave quantization"**: Process multiple query heads per program 5. **Use `evict_last` policy on Q load** so it stays resident 6. **Fuse the partition combine** if NP=1 7. **Tail handling for non-pow2 seq_len**: Need to make sure the masking works 8. **Handle 0-element partitions correctly**: For shape 4 (B=16, L=1535), with NP=2 partitions, partition 0 has 768 tokens, partition 1 has 767. With BLOCK_N=32, that means partition 1 covers blocks 0-23 plus a partial last block. We need to make sure the partition end clamp works correctly. 9. **Combine partition for "fast path"**: For small problems where BHkv is enough, fuse into a single kernel and skip the combine step. Let me also think about what could be wrong with the existing codex kernel: 1. The PAD_G is `max(16, _next_pow2(self.group_size))` -- for G=4, that's 16. For G=8, that's 16. Always 16. Why 16? Probably to satisfy `min_dot_size` requirements. With PAD_G=16, the dot is (16, 128) @ (128, 64) for BLOCK_N=64, which is fine. 2. The num_warps=4 with PAD_G=16 BLOCK_D=128: registers per warp is (16 * 128) = 2048 fp32 elements per warp, so 64 fp32 elements per thread (4 warps = 128 threads, 16 * 128 / 128 = 16 elements per thread for acc). That's reasonable. 3. For BLOCK_N=64, K is 128*64*2 = 16KB, V is also 16KB. With num_stages=3, total shared memory is 96KB which is over the 100KB SM limit. So Triton may use less than 3 stages. Let me also think about the pad_g trick. In the codex kernel, the dot is: ```python scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k), out_dtype=tl.float32) ``` where `q` is (PAD_G=16, BLOCK_D=128) and `k` is (BLOCK_N=64, BLOCK_D=128). After tl.trans, k is (128, 64). The dot is (16, 128) @ (128, 64) -> (16, 64). Then m_i is over the 16 axis, but we have g_mask to handle only the first GROUP_SIZE rows. Actually wait, looking at the codex kernel more carefully: ```python q = (q.to(tl.float32) * SCALE_LOG2E).to(tl.bfloat16) ``` This scales Q by log2e and casts back to bf16. Then `scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k), out_dtype=tl.float32)`. The dot is in bf16, output fp32. Then `m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(scores, axis=1))`. The scaling inside bf16 might cause precision loss for non-pow2 scale values. But log2e = 1.4426950408889634 is a single value and multiplying by it in fp32 first then casting back is fine. Now for the AV dot: ```python acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p.to(tl.bfloat16), v, out_dtype=tl.float32) ``` p is (PAD_G=16, BLOCK_N=64), cast to bf16. v is (BLOCK_N=64, BLOCK_D=128). Dot is (16, 64) @ (64, 128) -> (16, 128). Good. Actually wait, there might be a subtle issue. The PAD_G=16 padding means we have 16 rows but only 4 (or 8) are valid. The `tl.dot` operates on the full 16x16 tile, so even though the GQA group is only 4, we still execute the full 16 rows of compute. This is wasted compute but lets us use a larger dot tile for tensor core utilization. A potential issue: the alpha update `l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p, axis=1)` where l_i is (PAD_G,) so alpha must be (PAD_G,). And p has shape (PAD_G, BLOCK_N) -- axis=1 sum is fine. OK so the codex kernel is solid. Let me see if there are any optimizations I'm missing. Key question: **Can we reduce memory traffic below the floor?** The KV cache must be read once. K is L * Hkv * D * 2 bytes. V is the same. Total = 2 * B * L * Hkv * D * 2 = 4 * B * L * Hkv * D bytes per problem. The flops_formula is 4 * B * H * L * D = 4 * B * G * Hkv * L * D. Ratio: 4 * B * G * Hkv * L * D / 4 / (4 * B * L * Hkv * D) = G/4 flops/byte. For G=4 (B=8 H=32 Hkv=8), arithmetic intensity = 1 flop/byte. That's TINY. We're absolutely memory-bound. For G=8 (B=4 H=64 Hkv=8), arithmetic intensity = 2 flops/byte. Still tiny. So our goal is just to make sure we hit 100% of bandwidth on KV reads. Some ideas to improve memory throughput: 1. **Use vectorized loads**: Triton should already do this for contiguous data 2. **Use cp.async**: pipelined loads for overlapping memory and compute 3. **Use larger BLOCK_N** so each load does more work 4. **Avoid loading K and V together when possible** to reduce register pressure Actually wait - we're loading K and V separately. The layout is [K | V] packed, so K is at offset 0, V is at offset D. Each K load is contiguous BLOCK_N tokens x D elements. For BLOCK_N=64, D=128, that's 16KB per load. Let me also think about L2 cache utilization. With BLOCK_N=64 and the inner loop, we load 64 tokens at a time. After the program finishes, the next partition (different SM) needs the same KV cache. So L2 helps here only if multiple programs share KV data, which they don't (each (batch, kv_head, partition) is independent). Wait, but multiple kv_heads for the same batch can share K (same K, different V?). No, each kv_head has its own K and V. So the total bytes loaded = B * Hkv * L * D * 2 * 2 (K and V) = 4 * B * Hkv * L * D bytes. For shape 1 (B=8, L=1024, Hkv=8, D=128), that's 4 * 8 * 1024 * 8 * 128 = 32 MB. At 1.8 TB/s peak, this takes 32/1800 = 17.8 μs. The current best is 0.6637 * 1800 = 1194 GB/s. 32MB / 1194 GB/s = 27 μs. Hmm, so we're at 2.1x of the theoretical floor. Let me look at the prior result.json to get the actual times: Actually let me look at the benchmark.py output for the prior solution to get a sense of times:

That's wasteful in terms of load instructions but Triton may deduplicate. Wait, actually no. `tl.load(BT + b * NUM_PAGES + page_ids)` with `page_ids = page_base + offs_n // PAGE_SIZE`. For BLOCK_N=128, offs_n = [0, 1, ..., 127], and page_ids = page_base + [0,0,...,0,1,1,...,1,...,7,7,...,7]. So we load each of 8 pages' block_id 16 times. This is a non-coalesced pattern across the 128-wide load, which is bad for memory bandwidth. Actually the GPU coalesces loads: 32 threads in a warp will load consecutive elements. So a 128-wide load = 4 warps loading 32 elements each. With page_ids being [0,0,...,0,1,1,...,1,...], the addresses for the first warp are all 0 (16 threads load page 0, 16 threads load page 1). The hardware should coalesce these if it recognizes they're the same address. But CUDA's behavior is that each thread issues a load, and if the L1 cache line is the same, only one transaction is needed. So this is OK. But the main cost is that we're loading 128 elements from BT (out of which only 8 are unique), wasting 16x of the load instruction count. But these are just integer loads, not bf16 loads. Each iteration of the loop has: - 1 page_ids load (BLOCK_N int32 = 4 bytes per thread, 32 elements = 128 bytes = 1 cache line) - 1 K load (BLOCK_N * D bf16 = BLOCK_N*D*2 bytes) - 1 V load (BLOCK_N * D bf16 = BLOCK_N*D*2 bytes) - 1 dot Q*K (small) - 1 dot P*V (small) - Various masking For BLOCK_N=64 D=128, K and V are each 16KB. The page_ids within the 128-wide load are duplicated 16 times (8 unique values). Wait, this is interesting. The block_ids load is `tl.load(BT + b * NUM_PAGES + page_ids, mask=page_ids < NUM_PAGES, other=0)` with `page_ids = page_base + offs_n // PAGE_SIZE` and `offs_n = arange(0, BLOCK_N) = arange(0, 128)`. This is essentially 8 unique int32 loads repeated 16x. The hardware should coalesce within a warp (16 threads loading the same address) and issue one transaction. Between tokens, the offset is (block_id * 16 * 4 * 2D + page_off * 4 * 2D). For the same block_id and different page_offs, the offset is 4 * 2D = 512 bytes apart. stdout (1010 chars)
1	"""Roofline math: achieved TFLOPS / GB/s, peak fraction.
2	
3	FLOPS and bytes formulas come from the problem's `problem.yaml`. They are the
4	dense-equivalent algorithmic work; kernels that skip work (sparsity, early
5	exit) are still measured against the dense cost.
6	"""
7	from __future__ import annotations
8	
9	
10	def compute_tflops(flops: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
11	    """flops per invocation and wall time in ms -> TFLOPS."""
12	    if time_ms <= 0:
13	        return 0.0
14	    return flops / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e12
15	
16	
17	def compute_gbps(bytes_moved: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
18	    """bytes per invocation and wall time in ms -> GB/s."""
19	    if time_ms <= 0:
20	        return 0.0
21	    return bytes_moved / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e9
22	
23	
24	def peak_fraction(
25	    achieved: float,
26	    peak: float,
27	) -> float:
28	    """Return achieved / peak, clamped to [0, infinity)."""
29	    if peak <= 0:
30	        return 0.0
31	    return max(0.0, achieved / peak)
32

The slice `[..., 0, :]` and `[..., 1, :]` would need to materialize. Actually I think the cleanest way is to use two separate loads. The hardware can pipeline them. OK let me just write the code. OK now let me write the new solution. Here's my plan: 1. **Direct kernel (one kernel) for high-base cases (B*Hkv >= 192)** 2. **Split kernel (two kernels: split + combine) for low-base cases** 3. **Per-shape tuning**: BLOCK_N, num_warps, num_stages 4. **Smarter partition heuristic**: target 1-2 waves 5. **Cursor 2.5 style K/V loads** (K as (D, BLOCK_N), no trans) 6. **CUDA graph capture** Let me start writing. Actually let me think about one more optimization: **process multiple Q heads per K head via GQA grouping**. For G=4 (most shapes), we have 4 Q heads per KV head. The K and V are shared. If we process all 4 Q heads in one program, we get better K/V reuse. But we already do this! The `q` tile is (G, D) and we compute (G, D) @ (D, BLOCK_N) = (G, BLOCK_N) in one dot. So all 4 Q heads share the K and V loads. OK so we're already maximizing K/V reuse. One more thing: **what if we have only G=2 or G=1 cases**? Not in our shapes. All are G=4 or G=8. OK let me write the code. Wait, I should also check if there's any way to use TMA (Tensor Memory Accelerator) on Blackwell. Triton 3.6.0 has some TMA support. Triton's TMA support: - `tl.experimental.descriptor_load` for TMA loads - Requires a `TensorDescriptor` object created on host - Can do async bulk loads For our case, TMA would issue a single large load (e.g., 16 KB) instead of multiple smaller loads. This can reduce instruction count and improve memory throughput. But TMA descriptors need to be created per (shape, address), which is dynamic. We'd need to create them in the kernel, which is tricky. Triton has `tl.make_block_ptr` and `tl.advance` for block pointers. These can be combined with TMA in newer versions. Actually, let me focus on writing a clean Triton solution that I can verify works. TMA is a stretch goal. Let me write the solution. Here's the structure: ```python """Paged attention decode kernel - optimized for RTX PRO 6000 (SM120).""" import math import os import torch import torch.nn as nn try: import triton import triton.language as tl _HAS_TRITON = True except Exception: _HAS_TRITON = False _NUM_SM = 188 _LOG2E = 1.4426950408889634 _DISABLE_GRAPHS = os.environ.get("KBH_DISABLE_CUDA_GRAPHS", "0") == "1" @triton.jit def _split_kernel( Q, KV, BT, SL, Mp, Lp, Accp, qk_scale_log2e, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_kvb, stride_kvt, stride_kvh, stride_mpb, stride_mph, stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accp, stride_btb, tokens_per_part, G: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr, BLOCKS_PER_PART: tl.constexpr, PAD_G: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_kvh = tl.program_id(1) pid_p = tl.program_id(2) seq_b = tl.load(SL + pid_b) tok_start = pid_p * tokens_per_part tok_end = tl.minimum((pid_p + 1) * tokens_per_part, seq_b) offs_g = tl.arange(0, PAD_G) offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) offs_n = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N) g_mask = offs_g < G d_mask = offs_d < D h0 = pid_kvh * G q_ptrs = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + (h0 + offs_g[:, None]) * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :] q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0, eviction_policy="evict_last") m_i = tl.full((PAD_G,), -1.0e30, tl.float32) l_i = tl.zeros((PAD_G,), tl.float32) acc = tl.zeros((PAD_G, BLOCK_D), tl.float32) for i in range(BLOCKS_PER_PART): start_n = tok_start + i * BLOCK_N offs_n_local = start_n + offs_n mask_n = offs_n_local < tok_end page_slot = offs_n_local // P within = offs_n_local % P pages = tl.load(BT + pid_b * stride_btb + page_slot, mask=mask_n, other=0) tok_base = ( pages.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvb + within.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvt + pid_kvh * stride_kvh ) # K as (D, BLOCK_N): each row of K is a token's D-dim embedding k_ptrs = KV + tok_base[None, :] + offs_d[:, None] k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=d_mask[:, None] & mask_n[None, :], other=0.0, eviction_policy="evict_first") # V as (BLOCK_N, D) v_ptrs = KV + tok_base[:, None] + D + offs_d[None, :] v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=mask_n[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0, eviction_policy="evict_first") # QK = q @ k = (G, D) @ (D, BLOCK_N) = (G, BLOCK_N) s = tl.dot(q, k, out_dtype=tl.float32) * qk_scale_log2e s = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], s, -1.0e30) m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(s, axis=1)) alpha = tl.exp2(m_i - m_new) p = tl.exp2(s - m_new[:, None]) p = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], p, 0.0) l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p, axis=1) acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p.to(tl.bfloat16), v, out_dtype=tl.float32) m_i = m_new heads = h0 + offs_g ml_off = pid_b * stride_mpb + heads * stride_mph + pid_p tl.store(Mp + ml_off, m_i, mask=g_mask) tl.store(Lp + ml_off, l_i, mask=g_mask) acc_ptrs = ( Accp + pid_b * stride_accb + heads[:, None] * stride_acch + pid_p * stride_accp + offs_d[None, :] ) tl.store(acc_ptrs, acc, mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :]) @triton.jit def _combine_kernel( Mp, Lp, Accp, Out, stride_mpb, stride_mph, stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accp, stride_ob, stride_oh, NP, D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_P: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_h = tl.program_id(1) offs_p = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_P) offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) mask_p = offs_p < NP d_mask = offs_d < D base_ml = pid_b * stride_mpb + pid_h * stride_mph m = tl.load(Mp + base_ml + offs_p, mask=mask_p, other=-1.0e30) m_max = tl.max(m, axis=0) w = tl.exp2(m - m_max) w = tl.where(mask_p, w, 0.0) l = tl.load(Lp + base_ml + offs_p, mask=mask_p, other=0.0) L = tl.sum(w * l, axis=0) acc_ptrs = ( Accp + pid_b * stride_accb + pid_h * stride_acch + offs_p[:, None] * stride_accp + offs_d[None, :] ) acc = tl.load(acc_ptrs, mask=mask_p[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0) out = tl.sum(w[:, None] * acc, axis=0) / tl.maximum(L, 1e-30) tl.store(Out + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + offs_d, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=d_mask) @triton.jit def _direct_kernel( Q, KV, BT, SL, Out, qk_scale_log2e, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_kvb, stride_kvt, stride_kvh, stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_btb, G: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr, N_ITERS: tl.constexpr, PAD_G: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_kvh = tl.program_id(1) seq_b = tl.load(SL + pid_b) offs_g = tl.arange(0, PAD_G) offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) offs_n = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N) g_mask = offs_g < G d_mask = offs_d < D h0 = pid_kvh * G q_ptrs = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + (h0 + offs_g[:, None]) * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :] q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0, eviction_policy="evict_last") m_i = tl.full((PAD_G,), -1.0e30, tl.float32) l_i = tl.zeros((PAD_G,), tl.float32) acc = tl.zeros((PAD_G, BLOCK_D), tl.float32) for i in range(N_ITERS): start_n = i * BLOCK_N offs_n_local = start_n + offs_n mask_n = offs_n_local < seq_b page_slot = offs_n_local // P within = offs_n_local % P pages = tl.load(BT + pid_b * stride_btb + page_slot, mask=mask_n, other=0) tok_base = ( pages.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvb + within.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvt + pid_kvh * stride_kvh ) k_ptrs = KV + tok_base[None, :] + offs_d[:, None] k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=d_mask[:, None] & mask_n[None, :], other=0.0, eviction_policy="evict_first") v_ptrs = KV + tok_base[:, None] + D + offs_d[None, :] v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=mask_n[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0, eviction_policy="evict_first") s = tl.dot(q, k, out_dtype=tl.float32) * qk_scale_log2e s = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], s, -1.0e30) m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(s, axis=1)) alpha = tl.exp2(m_i - m_new) p = tl.exp2(s - m_new[:, None]) p = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], p, 0.0) l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p, axis=1) acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p.to(tl.bfloat16), v, out_dtype=tl.float32) m_i = m_new out = acc / l_i[:, None] out_ptrs = Out + pid_b * stride_ob + (h0 + offs_g[:, None]) * stride_oh + offs_d[None, :] tl.store(out_ptrs, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :]) ``` Wait, looking at this again, the Q scaling and the operations are: - Q is loaded as bf16 (G, D) - s = tl.dot(q, k) gives (G, BLOCK_N) in fp32 - s is multiplied by qk_scale_log2e - exp2 is used for softmax But the `s = tl.dot(q, k) * qk_scale_log2e` can lose precision if we multiply bf16 by fp32 (it would upcast to fp32). Then `s = tl.where(mask, s, -1e30)` and `exp2(s - m_new)` are in fp32. Good. Actually wait, the codex does: ```python q = (q.to(tl.float32) * SCALE_LOG2E).to(tl.bfloat16) scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k), out_dtype=tl.float32) ``` So they scale Q before the dot, then dot in bf16. This is more efficient (bf16 dot is faster than fp32 dot) but slightly less precise. The cursor 2.5 does the same: ```python q = (q.to(tl.float32) * SCALE_LOG2E).to(tl.bfloat16) scores = tl.dot(q, k, out_dtype=tl.float32) ``` So both pre-scale Q. Let me do the same. OK let me also think about: **what if I scale k instead of q**? Same effect. The choice doesn't matter much. **What if I scale the Q for the entire batch in a separate kernel**? Then the dot is un-scaled and we just exp2. We could pre-scale Q at init time and store it. But Q is per-call (could be different each call), so pre-scaling at init is wrong. We could pre-scale in the first kernel of the split (a Q-scale kernel). But that's an extra launch. The pre-scale-in-triton approach is fine. OK let me write the full solution. For the partition heuristic, let me think more carefully: ```python def _pick_num_partitions(B, Hkv, seq_len, block_n): base_blocks = B * Hkv if base_blocks >= 192: # Use direct (1 partition) - we have enough parallelism return 1 # Target 1-2 waves target_progs = 256 # ~1.36 waves np_ = max(1, target_progs // base_blocks) # Ensure partition_size is a multiple of block_n (no partial iters) max_np = (seq_len + block_n - 1) // block_n np_ = min(np_, max_np) return np_ ``` Wait, this gives 1.36 waves for any low-base case. Hmm. Actually let me think again. For base=32, target=256, NP=8. 32*8=256 progs, 1.36 waves. For base=64, target=256, NP=4. 64*4=256 progs, 1.36 waves. Let me also think about whether the per-prog work is reasonable. For shape 4 NP=8 BLOCK_N=64 partition=250: per-prog = 250*4*64*2 = 128 KB. For shape 0 NP=4 BLOCK_N=64 partition=256: per-prog = 256*4*128*2 = 262 KB. For shape 2 NP=8 BLOCK_N=64 partition=512: per-prog = 512*4*128*2 = 524 KB. For shape 3 NP=2 BLOCK_N=64 partition=768: per-prog = 768*4*128*2 = 786 KB. For shape 1 direct: per-prog = 2048*4*128*2 = 2.1 MB. For shape 4, per-prog is 128 KB. With 188 SMs concurrent, total = 188 * 128 KB = 24 MB in-flight. For 256 progs, 1.36 waves. Per wave = 24 MB. Time = 24 / 1800 = 13.3 μs per wave. 1.36 waves = 18.1 μs. Same as before! Hmm. The per-wave time is determined by per-prog-work * 188 / 1800. For shape 4, that's 128 KB * 188 / 1800 GB/s = 13.3 μs. With 1.36 waves, total = 18.1 μs. So reducing waves doesn't help if per-prog-work is the same. The only way to reduce time is to reduce per-prog-work (smaller partition). But smaller partition = more programs = more waves. So the optimal is some balance. The wave model says any balance gives the same time (floor + wave overhead). So we want to minimize wave overhead, which means fewer waves. Wait, that's not right. Let me re-think. For shape 4 NP=24 (4.08 waves), per-prog = 43 KB. Per wave = 188 * 43 = 8 MB. Time per wave = 8/1800 = 4.5 μs. Total = 4.08 * 4.5 = 18.4 μs. Matches observed 19.4. For shape 4 NP=8 (1.36 waves), per-prog = 128 KB. Per wave = 24 MB. Time per wave = 13.3 μs. Total = 1.36 * 13.3 = 18.1 μs. Same! So the wave model says any NP gives the same time. The actual differences are wave overhead. If wave overhead is 1 μs per wave (an arbitrary number), then: - NP=24: 4.08 * (4.5 + 1) = 22.4 μs - NP=8: 1.36 * (13.3 + 1) = 19.4 μs - NP=4: 0.68 * (26.7 + 1) = 18.8 μs Hmm NP=8 wins. Or maybe NP=4 if wave overhead is 0.5 μs. The real overhead per wave depends on hardware. For modern GPUs, it's small (maybe 100-500 ns). OK let me just pick NP=8 for shape 4 (or whatever gives 1-2 waves) and trust it'll be OK. Actually, let me look at this differently. The CUDA graph capture should reduce launch overhead. With CUDA graphs, each kernel launch is just a replay, which is much faster than the initial launch. So the per-wave overhead should be tiny. Let me look at the codex solution more carefully for the CUDA graph: ```python def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens): buffers = self._alloc_buffers(query.device, query.dtype) out = buffers[0] key = (query.data_ptr(), kv_cache.data_ptr(), block_table.data_ptr(), seq_lens.data_ptr()) graph = self._graph_cache.get(key) if graph is None: self._launch(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, buffers) torch.cuda.synchronize() graph = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph() with torch.cuda.graph(graph): self._launch(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, buffers) self._graph_cache[key] = graph graph.replay() return out ``` So the first call does a warmup launch, then captures the graph. Subsequent calls just replay. OK let me write the solution. I'll follow the codex structure but with my optimizations. Let me also think about: **should I use Triton's autotune**? Autotune can find the best config for each shape. But it adds compile time and may cause timeouts. For check.py, the timeout is 180s. If autotune tries 5 configs for each of 5 shapes = 25 compiles, that's risky. For benchmark.py, the time is less critical (we want fast runtime, not fast compile). Let me skip autotune and just hand-tune the configs. OK let me write the solution now. Here's the final design: 1. **Three kernels**: direct (high-base), split (low-base), combine. 2. **Direct**: For B*Hkv >= 256. BLOCK_N=128, num_warps=4, num_stages=2. 3. **Split**: For B*Hkv < 256. NP = max(1, 256 // base_blocks) to target ~256 progs. 4. **BLOCK_N**: 64 for D=128, 128 for D=64. 5. **num_warps=4, num_stages=2** for split (for D=128); num_stages=3 for D=64. 6. **PAD_G=16** for tensor core tile. 7. **Pre-scale Q by log2e**. 8. **K loaded as (D, BLOCK_N), V as (BLOCK_N, D)**. 9. **CUDA graph capture**. Let me also think about the partition_size rounding. If we round up to multiple of BLOCK_N, the inner loop is always full iters. No partial iters. But partition_size = seq_len / NP might not be a multiple of BLOCK_N. We can either: - Round up: partition_size = ceil(seq_len / NP / BLOCK_N) * BLOCK_N. Each partition covers slightly more than seq_len/NP. Total might exceed seq_len. The masking handles this. - Round down: partition_size = floor(seq_len / NP / BLOCK_N) * BLOCK_N. Last partition is smaller. The current codex kernel does: ```python partition_size = (seq_len + num_partitions - 1) // num_partitions partition_size = ((partition_size + block_n - 1) // block_n) * block_n ``` This rounds up to multiple of BLOCK_N. The last partition might be smaller than the others (it covers tokens [NP*partition_size, seq_len)). For the split kernel, we have `partition_size` and `BLOCKS_PER_PART = ceil(partition_size / BLOCK_N)`. The inner loop runs BLOCKS_PER_PART times, with masking for the last iter. OK let me just write the code. I'll follow the proven design with my tweaks. One more thought: **use `tl.dot` with `input_precision="ieee"` for the AV dot** to ensure maximum precision. The QK dot doesn't need this (it's just a dot product, bf16 is fine). The AV dot is more sensitive because errors compound. Actually, let me check. The codex uses default precision for both dots. The cursor 2.5 also uses default. The default for bf16 is high precision (matches IEEE 754 for bf16). For fp16 with `input_precision="ieee"`, it forces FP32 accumulation. But for bf16, accumulation is always fp32 (no FP16 acc in modern GPUs). So precision shouldn't be an issue. Let me use default. OK writing the solution now. +"""Paged attention decode kernel for RTX PRO 6000 (SM120 Blackwell, GDDR7, 1.8 TB/s).
+
+Single-query GQA decode is bandwidth-bound. The ceiling is "stream the packed
+KV cache exactly once" and the design is FlashDecoding split-K:
+
+  Phase 1 (split): one program per (batch, kv_head, partition). Streams its slice
+    of the paged KV cache for one kv_head, shared across the GROUP_SIZE query
+    heads that map to that kv_head. Online softmax in the exp2 domain (log2e
+    folded into the QK scale). bf16 tensor-core dots with fp32 accumulation.
+    KV read with `evict_first` so the streamed cache lines never displace the
+    Q tile (which we keep with `evict_last`) from L2.
+  Phase 2 (combine): one program per (batch, head) does the log-sum-exp
+    reduction across that head's partitions and writes the bf16 output.
+
+For high-parallelism problems (B*Hkv large) the split is unnecessary; a single
+fused kernel (NP=1) is launched that does the full sequence in registers.
+
+`forward` captures a CUDA graph keyed on the input data_ptrs so the benchmark's
+40x replay of the same input tensors skips per-launch overhead.
+"""
+import math
+import os
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+
+try:
+    import triton
+    import triton.language as tl
+
+    _HAS_TRITON = True
+except Exception:  # pragma: no cover - triton always present in the harness
+    _HAS_TRITON = False
+
+# RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell Workstation: GB202, 188 SMs, 96MB L2.
+_NUM_SM = 188
+_LOG2E = 1.4426950408889634
+_DISABLE_GRAPHS = os.environ.get("KBH_DISABLE_CUDA_GRAPHS", "0") == "1"
+_NEG_LARGE = -1.0e30
+
+
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# Triton kernels
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+
+if _HAS_TRITON:
+
+    @triton.jit
+    def _split_kernel(
+        Q,                      # (B, H, D)                bf16
+        KV,                     # (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2D) bf16 [K|V]
+        BT,                     # (B, max_blocks)          int32
+        SL,                     # (B,)                     int32
+        Mp,                     # (B, H, NP)               fp32 partial max
+        Lp,                     # (B, H, NP)               fp32 partial L
+        Accp,                   # (B, H, NP, D)            fp32 partial acc
+        qk_scale_log2e,         # (1/sqrt(d)) * log2(e)    fp32 scalar
+        stride_qb, stride_qh,
+        stride_kvb, stride_kvt, stride_kvh,
+        stride_mpb, stride_mph,
+        stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accp,
+        stride_btb,
+        tokens_per_part,
+        G: tl.constexpr,
+        D: tl.constexpr,
+        P: tl.constexpr,
+        BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr,
+        BLOCKS_PER_PART: tl.constexpr,
+        PAD_G: tl.constexpr,
+        BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
+    ):
+        pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+        pid_kvh = tl.program_id(1)
+        pid_p = tl.program_id(2)
+
+        seq_b = tl.load(SL + pid_b)
+        tok_start = pid_p * tokens_per_part
+        tok_end = tl.minimum((pid_p + 1) * tokens_per_part, seq_b)
+
+        offs_g = tl.arange(0, PAD_G)
+        offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
+        offs_n = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)
+        g_mask = offs_g < G
+        d_mask = offs_d < D
+
+        # Q tile (G, D) -> (PAD_G, BLOCK_D) bf16, with `evict_last` so the
+        # pre-scaled Q tile stays resident for all inner iters.
+        h0 = pid_kvh * G
+        q_ptrs = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + (h0 + offs_g[:, None]) * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
+        q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=g_mask[:, None] & d_mask[None, :], other=0.0,
+                    eviction_policy="evict_last")
+        # Pre-scale by log2e so the inner loop uses exp2 (one mma-less mulf saved
+        # per element). fp32 multiply then cast back keeps the Q tensor as bf16
+        # so the dot binds bf16 tensor cores.
+        q = (q.to(tl.float32) * qk_scale_log2e).to(tl.bfloat16)
+
+        m_i = tl.full((PAD_G,), _NEG_LARGE, tl.float32)
+        l_i = tl.zeros((PAD_G,), tl.float32)
+        acc = tl.zeros((PAD_G, BLOCK_D), tl.float32)
+
+        # Constexpr trip count -> no data-dependent control flow. Slots past
+        # tok_end are masked off; over-covered bytes are predicated.
+        for i in range(BLOCKS_PER_PART):
+            start_n = tok_start + i * BLOCK_N
+            offs_n_local = start_n + offs_n
+            mask_n = offs_n_local < tok_end
+
+            page_slot = offs_n_local // P
+            within = offs_n_local % P
+            pages = tl.load(BT + pid_b * stride_btb + page_slot, mask=mask_n, other=0)
+            tok_base = (
+                pages.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvb
+                + within.to(tl.int64) * stride_kvt
+                + pid_kvh * stride_kvh
+            )
+
+            # K loaded in (BLOCK_D, BLOCK_N) layout -- i.e., transposed wrt the
+            # natural (token, dim) order -- so the QK dot needs no tl.trans.
+            k_ptrs = KV + tok_base[None, :] + offs_d[:, None]
+            k = tl.load(
+                k_ptrs,
+                mask=d_mask[:, None] & mask_n[None, :],
+                other=0.0,
+                eviction_policy="evict_first",
+            )
+            # V loaded in (BLOCK_N, BLOCK_D) for the AV dot.
+            v_ptrs = KV + tok_base[:, None] + D + offs_d[None, :]
+            v = tl.load(
+                v_ptrs,
+                mask=mask_n[:, None] & d_mask[None, :],
+                other=0.0,
+                eviction_policy="evict_first",
+            )
+
+            # s = (G, D) @ (D, BLOCK_N) = (G, BLOCK_N) fp32
+            s = tl.dot(q, k, out_dtype=tl.float32)
+            s = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], s, _NEG_LARGE)
+
+            m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(s, axis=1))
+            alpha = tl.exp2(m_i -

... (14937 more chars)

"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.

All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.

Methodology:
  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.

Notes / known biases not addressed here:
  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
    "compiled" baseline policy.
  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
    instrumentation if you ever care.
